<text>Been scouting for a good place to buy tamales for my employees. Normally buy about 10 or so dozen monthly. I was told of Luna's Bakery, so decided to try this place. I initially bought 1 & 1/2 dozen (half chicken, half red pork) for my family just to try them out. I spent $28.00 bucks. What a SHAME. The taste of the masa (dough) was decent, but what was terribly disappointing was the meat inside. After trying the first one, I noticed there was almost no meat or sauce, so instead of enjoying these tamales, my family and I spent the time inspecting them. LITERALLY, every single tamale had- and I do not exaggerate- about 4 or 5 Single Strands of chicken or pork about an inch long. I am sure, and I do not mean this sarcastically, they most likely use less than a chicken thigh to make a dozen tamales. I don't like to waste my time writing reviews but I was a bit angry with this place. What a bunch of miserable merchants. What a RIP OFF. Not even close to one star. I don't recommend this place; try a fast food place instead; my money would have been better spent buying tamales at Del Taco.<//text><resp>None</resp><rating>1</rating><user>107283811044814347943<//user>< user_name>

< text>
Small but clean studio (only 3 rooms) with friendly and knowledgeable staff. After two weeks, I'm hooked on the classes and teachers here are thoughtful, and willing to answer questions before and after class.

Bathrooms are nicely stocked and from what I've witnessed, after every shuffle the showers are wiped clean every time.

Cold eucalyptus towels are always available. I've yet to go during the daytime but this level of quality has been consistent for me every time I go during the afternoon and evenings.

They offer two hour validation at all hours.

The class heat from what I've noticed depends on the instructor but they don't mind if you need to step out for air or water. Also, heads up, Barre, Sculpt and Power will kick your butt.

I started with a free week trial and now I am a member and for me, totally worth it for the experience, the sense of community I feel there, the amenities, and of course for the instructors and yoga classes themselves. Do yourself a favor, get the free week trial at the very least.

Last tip: Get their app! You'll be guaranteed a spot in class, as long as you show up on time. You can view all the classes, their time and instructor too.</text>

< Review>
I loved this place before COVID, but I just took my first class since it reopened and cannot say enough about how well they handled opening during this pandemic. There was clear signage everywhere indicating social distancing, temperature checks, masks are required until you got to your designated space, they provide clean mats and towels so no one is bringing in anything from the outside, if you needed an iPad to sign something it got wiped with a disinfectant wipe in front of you, there's plexiglass separating you from the people at the front desk and the whole place smells like natural disinfectant... they thought of everything. < text>
Me and my partner are trying Hot 8 Yoga free for a week. Thank you for this opportunity.

This review is for Sherman Oaks location.
I will start with the pros since I like to be positive. It is a nice facility, looks new, modern and clean. Our first class there was with Marja L and we loved her! She would come to us and make corrections and help us make adjustments when needed which is highly appreciated and I think every instructor should do. The point is to do these positions correctly as much as you can and sometimes it is hard to adjust yourself. I love the hot fusion classes even tho they tend to be all the same every time which makes it a bit pointless to come to class. A little variety would be nice.

Now with the cons:
This is my personal opinion but I think if they are offering a free week that should come with free rentals (towel, mat if you need it) It is a bit unpleasant to go for your free class and having to pay $5 or more to rent the mat, towel etc. Give away 2 or 3 classes instead of a week but make it a nice experience all the way.
On the same note Patrick D was at the register and since we were a bit late and we left our wallets in the car he was a pretty rude and kept pointing out that the mat and towel are rentals and we HAVE TO PAY! We got that the first time there was no need to make us feel like criminals... it really ruined our whole experience and was absolutely unnecessary.
The next class we took was on a weekday - this was a very unpleasant experience since the locker rooms are way too small to accommodate the huge crowd of people that come out of class all at once and there are ONLY 5 SHOWERS! This is absolutely unacceptable. I definitely won‚Äôt be paying $200 a month to wait for a shower when I am all wet after class and I can‚Äôt even get to my locker. Big disappointment - I ended up going home in my wet clothes because I could not deal with the chaos in the ladies locker room!
The second class we took was Power 1 which said the temperature is lower but it was not - way hotter than the hot fusion. We told the instructor and he tried to tell us it was because we were at the end of the room and it is good for us. Well if the end of the room gets hot maybe there should be a ventilation system to cool down that side of the room - just a suggestion. There were also way too many people in this class for the size of the room - considering mats and distance needed to enjoy your workout. There should be a cap to how many people can sign up for a specific class/studio so it can be enjoyable without anyone being crammed in the corner.
And now the fun part - at the end we had to do 2 validations - one was on the 8th floor??? I have never seen anything like that?! So my partner had to run to the 8th floor validate out ticket and then go back to the studio for a second validation. Well maybe they should get another machine LIKE the one on the 8th floor?!
We definitely won‚Äôt be paying $200 a month for pretty much the same classes with too many people and not big enough facility to accommodate that! We won‚Äôt be returning to this location either.</text>

< user>
106647296755432241246< /user>
<name>Jessica Lewis<//name><time>1504735591021</time><Rate>4<//Rate>< text>
I am truly loving this place! After our free Yelp class in January of this year, a whole 7 months went by before I went back for my free week. I took 6 classes that week and made sure to get good use out of it. And boy am I glad I did! I loved them all! I ended up getting a package of classes to continue my practice, and I love the fact that their packages do not expire - huge win as some places basically force you to use them up or loose them. I appreciate being able to spread out this pack based on when my schedule and budget allows.

So now for the nitty gritty...THE HEAT!

Look people, it's hot as Hades up in this place! I mean most classes are over 100 degrees but I promise you get used to it. Drink a ton of water the day before if you're going to a morning class or throughout the day for an evening class and that helps a lot. Just know it's hot AF but it's tolerable!

Try them all, but read the description. There was only one class (maybe it was the teacher, not sure), that I didn't really care for because it was just too advanced and I couldn't keep up. But I finished it! I love Yoga Sculpt with Marie K - you will be sore the next day! And I have truly grown to love Yoga Power Fusion - this class is perfect if you want to avoid inversions or pressure on your shoulders/wrists. There's not as much floor work and you can really work on your balance. As a dancer Yoga Barre is also really good.

They validate for 2-hours and if you come after 5:45 during the week or anytime on weekends you don't have to worry about going all the way up to the 9th floor to park.

Really happy to find a place to incorporate yoga into my weekly routine. Thanks Hot 8 Yoga!< /text>

< Text>
This is my "go to" spot for a healthy pick-up dinner. The chicken Tikka and fried white fish are my two favs. My husband really likes the chicken stew. It's a tomato based stew. The fried chicken cutlet is always moist and perfectly crunchy.  The rice is made with saffron, I  believe and it's so fluffy. The salad and veggies are always crisp. For the love of pickled food, the cabbage is great!

Simple, delicious and unique!

Btw, cash only

<review>If it weren't for a cheap food article published in the San Diego Reader newspaper, I wouldn't have found out that traditional Iraqi breakfast is served at Sagmani. This restaurant is located in an isolated and unassuming strip mall with "Mediterranean cuisine" and "Best kabobs in town" posters decorating the storefront. Sagmani is an ethnic hole in the wall, the type that's open for breakfast but with no morning menu provided. All of the early bird customers were Middle Eastern.

When I entered the establishment, I asked the server about my options for breakfast. She mentioned something about an "Iraqi omelete". I read that staples of Iraqi breakfast include eggs and bread in a dip, but I wanted something slightly different. I told her that I wanted to eat ful, or fava beans, which is one of my favorite Middle Eastern breakfast dishes. Perhaps she was cautious not to offend a foreigner, so she went into the kitchen to get someone who could help me out. A minute later, I was greeted by Mr. Sagmani himself, the chef and owner. He asked how I typically eat my breakfast and explained how he would cook it. Then off to the kitchen he went.

Chef Sagmani personally brought out my order and beamed with pleasure as he witnessed a foreigner about to eat breakfast cooked the same way as it is at his hometown in Iraq. The dish he presented was called "tishrib baghela bdehan", which consists of a thick slice of fried egg covering a bed of whole fava beans and mixed with torn pieces of Iraqi flatbread. On the side, the condiment plate was just as big as the main course, filled with olives, white onions, lime, and some type of mustard-like relish.

Out of all the Middle Eastern dishes I've eaten before, this breakfast combo was probably the least approachable. Not to say that Sagmani's cooking was horrible, the presentation and freshness of ingredients were to high standards, but the dish just had an acquired taste for a Western palate. It was very tangy and bitter since the beans and thick bread were soaked with strong olive oil. There was hardly any salt added, and the dish composed of many sharp and sour flavors that took a while to get used to. The flavors seemed to be closer to the food from Turkey than Iran, the two neighbors of Iraq.

Although most ingredients in "tishrib baghela bdehan" were familiar, it was the first time they were assembled into this unique combination. Each element tasted fine when eaten individually, but I couldn't imagine how I could stuff down large beans, egg, softened bread, ripe olives, and onions in the same bite. The complimentary black tea that Iraqis drink for breakfast helped wash down the sourness of the olive oil and my bad breathe thanks to the onions. Overall, this Iraqi breakfast was rich on the carbs and protein, so it's the heavy type that you'd want to eat when you need energy later.

On the way out, I noticed that Mr. Sagmani also specializes in grilling kabobs. Beef or chicken kabobs are available for $1.25 a piece, and it includes a small side salad. I wonder if Mr. Sagmani makes much profit from selling this! I also realized that other customers were ordering the lentil soup, which is another Iraqi breakfast favorite. I would try that next time instead, since it's significantly lighter.<//review><pictures>None<//pictures><Time>1450645806834</Time>< rating>
4< /rating>

Jo Squire< /Name>
<time>1506987285332< /time><rate>1< /rate>< Review>
Do not trust this company!!!
They tried to make us sign contracts that had missing sections, or incorrect information.
They never explained the broker fee as a broker fee until the very last moment when they legally had to disclose this in writing.
They tried to make us sign saying that they'd given us the insurance brochure from the government of California. When we asked to see this brochure, they did not even have a copy in the office!!
After spending 3 hours in there, having paid first before signing papers we wanted to cancel the policy and they said they couldn't reverse the credit card payment, only head office could do this. We ended up cancelling our credit card with our bank, as we read all the reviews on consumer affairs about how untrustryworthy they were. And true to that, a few days later head office called asking us for new payment details as the credit card failed!
Do not trust any of these Google reviews. They pay people to write a good review to receive a $60 discount (we did it).
We cannot stress how much these guys will do anything for their broker fee. You'll end up with a void policy if you go with these guys.
Also by signing with this company, you must agree for them to sell your phone number and email for marketing purposes. This is a condition of the policy.
All in all, these guys are absolute crooks and I wouldn't trust trust them any further than I could throw them...and I'm a pretty bad thrower! For more accurate reviews, go to consumer affairs where positive reviews are not rewarded. The government really needs to regulate the industry and push out crooks like this. We'd recommend going with a company that doesn't use brokers (e.g. Geico), you'll pay much less, understand what you are paying for, and be in and out of the office in half an hour. Don't waste your time with these guys!</Review>

<Pictures>None</Pictures>< review>
I love this store. I go there for Magic the Gathering products. Mike always has a good selection of accessories for tcg's. And while I don't play table top games, it seems like he's got a good selection of things like miniatures, paints and accessories for table top gaming as well..

What impresses me most is that the prices of his sealed Magic products are so competitive. You can get a booster box, packs and other sealed products for pretty cheap.

The only downside I would say is Mike doesn't deal in singles. If you are looking to buy single MTG, YGO, or Pok√©mon cards you'll have to go somewhere else. As for everything else, Mike either has it, or he can get it.

When we can get back to playing in stores. His store is fun to play at as well; great crowd, clean bathroom, the new store arrangement is excellent to. If you are into physical gaming like trading cards, table top or board games, Launchpad is a great place to shop at!< /review>

< Text>
After reading what others have posted, I was somewhat reluctant about stopping by to look at their ATV's and UTV's.  I was primarily interested in the Kymco line of quads.  After researching online what dealers in California carry the Kymco line, Salinas Motorcycle Center had the most Kymco inventory in stock.  So I took the chance last Friday and drove over while spending a couple of days in Monterey.

Well, I was pleasantly surprised.  They have a large inventory of bikes on their showroom floor.  I wasn't in there very long when I was approached by a salesman by the name of Martin.  He was very knowledgeable on the Kymco quad that I came in to look at.  Martin was very helpful, not pushy at all or trying to make a sale.  He answered all my questions.   After a while, he left and let me look and compare models on my own without him breathing down my neck.  Another employee (Hunter) came over and asked if I had any questions. He went on to say he was a mechanic there and told me about Kymco engine and component quality.  Hunter shared with me that he was one of the mechanics.

On my way out, I was approached by another sales person who was moving bikes around.  He asked me what I was interested in and began talking with me about other brands of bikes they carry.

So, about 40 minutes and 3 employees later, I did not experience any of the negative issues others have reported.  In light of the excellent customer service I received from 3 different employees, I only felt it was fair that I share my experience and leave a positive review.< /Text>
